## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of chemical kinetics â€” determining the rate law. Most rate laws express dA/dt purely as a function of A, but time-explicit dependence may arise from external forcing, photochemistry, or coupled species eliminated via time dependence.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of single species)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with back reaction from product)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic growth with saturation)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding kinetics)
- Parallel pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous reaction pathways)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (linearly time-modulated rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) â†’ classical rate law dA/dt = k*A^n; if t appears explicitly, suspect external forcing or eliminated coupled species
- Negative dA_dt with positive A â†’ consumption reaction (decay); sign of leading coefficient indicates consumption vs production
- Rational functions of A â†’ enzyme/surface catalysis mechanisms where active sites saturate
- Integer vs fractional power of A â†’ elementary reaction step vs complex/effective mechanism
- Linear dA_dt vs A relationship â†’ first-order kinetics, exponential decay solution; quadratic â†’ second-order, hyperbolic solution
- Product of A and (constant - A) terms â†’ reversible or autocatalytic reactions with conservation constraint
- Sum of power-law terms in A â†’ parallel competing reaction pathways with different molecularities
- Concentration appearing in denominator â†’ inhibition or saturation effects from intermediate species
- Time multiplied by concentration â†’ induction period or catalyst activation/deactivation phenomena
- Polynomial in A with specific sign pattern â†’ complex mechanism reduced via quasi-steady-state approximation on intermediates
